25:T5a00,<entryFree id="n9160" key="حَمَلَهُ" type="main">     
                  <form>       
                     <itype>1</itype>        
                     <orth orig="" extent="full" lang="ar">حَمَلَهُ</orth>
                     <orth extent="full" lang="ar">حمل</orth>
                     <orth extent="full" lang="ar">حمله</orth>
                     <orth extent="full" lang="ar">حملة</orth>
                  </form>, aor.      
    <form n="infl">       
                     <orth orig="Bi" lang="ar">حَمِلَ</orth>
                  </form>, inf. n. <foreign lang="ar">حَمْلٌ</foreign> (S, Mgh, Msb, K, &amp;c., in some copies of the S <foreign lang="ar">حِمْلٌ</foreign>) and <foreign lang="ar">حُمْلَانٌ</foreign>, (Mgh, K,) <hi rend="ital">He bore it, carried it, took it up and carried it, conveyed it,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">carried it off</hi> or <hi rend="ital">away,</hi> (MA,) <foreign lang="ar">عَلَى ظَهْرِهِ</foreign> (S, MA,) <hi rend="ital">upon his back,</hi> or <foreign lang="ar">عَلَى رَأْسِهِ</foreign> 
                  <hi rend="ital">upon his head;</hi> (MA;) and   
      <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n9160-1" target="احتملهُ" n="1" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar"/></foreign> signifies the same: (Msb, K:) or the latter is used in relation to an object inconsiderable and small in comparison with that in relation to which the former is used; as in the saying of En-Nábighah, (TA,) <quote>
                     <L>
                        <foreign lang="ar">إِنَّا ٱقْتَسَمْنَا خُطَّتَيْنَا بَيْنَنَا</foreign>
                     </L> 
                     <L><foreign lang="ar">فَحَمَلْتَ بَرَّةَ <ref cref="n9160-2" target="وَٱحْتَمَلْتُ" n="2" type="5" subtype="TFSO" lang="ar"/>فَجَارِ</foreign>
                     </L> 
                  </quote> [<hi rend="ital">Verily we have divided our two qualities between us, and thou hast borne</hi> as thy share <hi rend="ital">goodness, and I have borne</hi> as my share <hi rend="ital">wickedness</hi>]. (TA * in the present art., and S and TA &amp;c. in arts. <foreign lang="ar">بر</foreign> and <foreign lang="ar">فجر</foreign>.) Hence, in the Kur [xx. 100], <foreign lang="ar">فَإِنَّهُ</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">يَحْمِلُ يَوْمَ القِيَامَةِ وِزْرًا</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">He shall bear, on the day of resurrection, a heavy burden</hi>]. (TA.) Hence also, in the Kur [vii. 189], <foreign lang="ar">حَمَلَتْ حَمْلًا خَفِيفًا</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">She bore a light burden</hi>]; (S, TA;) i. e., [as some say,] the seminal fluid. (TA.) Hence also, in the Kur [xxix. 60], <foreign lang="ar">وَكَأَيِّنْ مِنْ دَابَّةٍ لَا تَحْمِلُ</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">رِزْقَهَا</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">And how many a beast</hi> is there that <hi rend="ital">does not bear its sustenance !</hi>], meaning, <assumedtropical>(assumed tropical:)</assumedtropical>  <hi rend="ital">does not provide its sustenance,</hi> but is sustained by God. (TA.) <foreign lang="ar">يَحْمِلُ الحَطَبَ</foreign> [lit. <hi rend="ital">He carries firewood</hi>], <pb n="647"/> (A in art. <foreign lang="ar">حطب</foreign>,) or <foreign lang="ar">الحَطَبَ الرَّطْبَ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">juicy,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">fresh, firewood</hi>], (Er-Rághib, TA,) means <tropical>(tropical:)</tropical>  <hi rend="ital">he goes about with calumny,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">slander.</hi> (A in art. <foreign lang="ar">حطب</foreign>, and Er-Rághib * and TA. *)          <sense type="b" n="2">-b2-</sense>  <foreign lang="ar">حَمَلَهُ عَلَى</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">الدَّابَّة</foreign>, (Msb, TA,) aor.      
    <form n="infl">       
                     <orth orig="Bi" lang="ar">حَمِلَ</orth>
                  </form>, (TA,) inf. n. <foreign lang="ar">حَمْلٌ</foreign>, (Msb, TA,) [<hi rend="ital">He carried him,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">mounted him,</hi> (namely, a man, Msb) <hi rend="ital">upon the beast;</hi> as also   
      <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n9160-3" target="احتملهُ" n="3" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar"/></foreign>.] And <foreign lang="ar">حَمَلَهُ</foreign> [alone] <hi rend="ital">He gave him a beast upon which to ride.</hi> (T, TA. [See Kur ix. 93.]) <foreign lang="ar">أَحْمَلَهُ</foreign> is not used in this sense. (T, TA.)          <sense type="b" n="3">-b3-</sense>  See also 4.          <sense type="b" n="4">-b4-</sense>  <foreign lang="ar">حَمَلَتِ المَرْأَةُ</foreign>, aor.      
    <form n="infl">       
                     <orth orig="Bi" lang="ar">حَمِلَ</orth>
                  </form>, (K,) inf. n. <foreign lang="ar">حَمْلٌ</foreign>, (TA,) <tropical>(tropical:)</tropical>  <hi rend="ital">The woman became pregnant,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">conceived:</hi> (K, TA:) and <foreign lang="ar">حَمَلَتْ وَلَدَهَا</foreign> 
                  <hi rend="ital">She became pregnant with,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">conceived, her child:</hi> (Msb:) one should not say, <foreign lang="ar">حَمَلَتْ بِهِ</foreign>; or this is rare; (K;) or one should not say this, but it is frequently said; (IJ, TA;) [for] as <foreign lang="ar">حَمَلَتْ</foreign> is syn. with <foreign lang="ar">عَلِقَتْ</foreign>, (Msb, TA,) and the latter is trans. by means of <foreign lang="ar">بِ</foreign> the former is thus made trans., (TA,) therefore one says, <foreign lang="ar">حَمَلَتْ بِهِ فِى لَيْلَةِ</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">كَذَا وَفِى مَوْضِعِ كَذَا</foreign>, meaning <hi rend="ital">She became pregnant with him,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">conceived him, in such a night, and in such a place.</hi> (Msb.) <foreign lang="ar">حَمَلَتْ</foreign> is also said of a ewe or she-goat, and of a female beast of prey, [and app. of any female,] accord. to IAar; meaning <assumedtropical>(assumed tropical:)</assumedtropical>  <hi rend="ital">She was,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">became, in the first stage of pregnancy.</hi> (TA.)          <sense type="b" n="5">-b5-</sense>  <foreign lang="ar">حَمَلَتِ الشَّجَرَةُ</foreign>, inf. n. <foreign lang="ar">حَمْلٌ</foreign>, <assumedtropical>(assumed tropical:)</assumedtropical>  <hi rend="ital">The tree</hi> [<hi rend="ital">bore,</hi> or] <hi rend="ital">produced,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">put forth, its fruit.</hi> (Msb.)          <sense type="b" n="6">-b6-</sense>  <foreign lang="ar">حَمَلَ بِدَيْنٍ</foreign>, and <foreign lang="ar">بِدِيَةٍ</foreign>, inf. n. <foreign lang="ar">حَمَالَةٌ</foreign>, <assumedtropical>(assumed tropical:)</assumedtropical>  [<hi rend="ital">He bore,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">took upon himself, the responsibility,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">he was,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">became, responsible, for a debt,</hi> and <hi rend="ital">a bloodwit:</hi>] (Msb:) [for] <foreign lang="ar">حَمَلَ بِهِ</foreign>, aor.      
    <form n="infl">       
                     <orth orig="Bi" lang="ar">حَمِلَ</orth>
                  </form>, inf. n. <foreign lang="ar">حَمَالَةٌ</foreign>, signifies <foreign lang="ar">كَفَلَ</foreign>. (S, * K.) And <foreign lang="ar">حَمَلَ الحَمَالَةَ</foreign> and

    <form n="infl">       
                     <orth orig="Bi" lang="ar">حَمِلَ</orth>
                  </form>, inf. n. <foreign lang="ar">حَمْلٌ</foreign>, a phrase often used in lexicology and grammar, <assumedtropical>(assumed tropical:)</assumedtropical>  <hi rend="ital">He made,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">held, a word,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">an expression, to accord in form,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">in meaning,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">syntactically, with another word,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">expression.</hi> One says, <foreign lang="ar">يُحْمَلُ عَلَى الأَكْثَرِ</foreign> <assumedtropical>(assumed tropical:)</assumedtropical>  <hi rend="ital">It</hi> (a word) <hi rend="ital">is made to accord in form with</hi> those words with which it may be compared that constitute <hi rend="ital">the greater number:</hi> thus one says of <foreign lang="ar">رَحْمَانُ</foreign>, which is made to accord in form with words of the measure <foreign lang="ar">فَعْلَانُ</foreign>, though it has not a fem. of the measure <foreign lang="ar">فَعْلَى</foreign>, in preference to <foreign lang="ar">فَعْلَانٌ</foreign>, because words of the measure <foreign lang="ar">فَعْلَانُ</foreign> are more numerous than those of the measure <foreign lang="ar">فَعْلَانٌ</foreign>. And <foreign lang="ar">يُحْمَلُ</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">عَلَى نَقِيضِهِ</foreign> <assumedtropical>(assumed tropical:)</assumedtropical>  <hi rend="ital">It</hi> (a word) <hi rend="ital">is made to accord in form with its contrary in meaning:</hi> thus <foreign lang="ar">عِجَافٌ</foreign>, an anomalous pl. of <foreign lang="ar">أَعْحَفُ</foreign>, is made to accord. in form with <foreign lang="ar">سِمَانٌ</foreign>, a regular pl. of <foreign lang="ar">سَمِينٌ</foreign>. And <foreign lang="ar">يَحمَلُ عَلَى المَعْنَى</foreign> <assumedtropical>(assumed tropical:)</assumedtropical>  <hi rend="ital">It</hi> (a word) <hi rend="ital">is made to accord syntactically with its meaning:</hi> and <foreign lang="ar">يُحْمَلُ عَلَى</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">اللَّفْظِ</foreign> <assumedtropical>(assumed tropical:)</assumedtropical>  <hi rend="ital">It is made to accord syntactically with its grammatical character:</hi> the former is said when, in a sentence, we make a mase. word fem., and the contrary, because the meaning allows us to substitute a fem. syn. for the masc. word, and a masc. syn. for the fem. word: for ex., it is said in the Kur vi. 78, <foreign lang="ar">فَلَمَّا رَأَى الشَّمْسَ بَازِغَةً قَالَ هٰذَا</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">رَبِّى</foreign> “ And when he saw the sun rising, he said, This is my Lord: ” here (by saying <foreign lang="ar">بازغة</foreign>) <foreign lang="ar">الشمس</foreign> is first made to accord syntactically with its grammatical character (<foreign lang="ar">تُحْمَلُ عَلَى اللَّفْظِ</foreign>); and then (by saying <foreign lang="ar">هٰذَا</foreign> instead of <foreign lang="ar">هٰذِهِ</foreign>) it is made to accord syntactically with its meaning (<foreign lang="ar">تُحْمَلُ عَلَى</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">المَعْنَى</foreign>), which is <foreign lang="ar">الجِرْم</foreign> or the like: this is allowable; but the reverse in respect of order is of weak authority; because the meaning is of more importance than the grammatical character of the word. (Collected from the Kull pp. 156 and 157, and other works.)]          <sense type="b" n="21">-b21-</sense>  <foreign lang="ar">حَمَلَهُ أَحْسَنَ مَحْيَلٍ</foreign> <assumedtropical>(assumed tropical:)</assumedtropical>  [<hi rend="ital">He put the best construction upon it;</hi> namely, a saying: <foreign lang="ar">محمل</foreign> being here an inf. n.].
